        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1063235637">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12333083473516636228">I was disappointed in this, Landvik's latest. It was about 200 pages too long and corny as all get-out. Interesting characters, but smarmy writing, syrupy, clichéd, contrived. Plot twists you could spot a mile away—quick, everyone pile into the car with the pregnant woman for a high speed chase! Oh what a shock, she goes into labor!<br /><br />I skimmed through the last part, intent on finishing but not really interested. Not in the same class as <a title="Patty Jane's House of Curl by Lorna Landvik" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16451.Patty_Jane_s_House_of_Curl">Patty Jane's House of Curl</a> or <a title="Your Oasis on Flame Lake by Lorna Landvik" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16450.Your_Oasis_on_Flame_Lake">Your Oasis on Flame Lake</a>. Apart</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12333083473516636228">I was disappointed in this, Landvik's latest. It was about 200 pages too long and corny as all get-out. Interesting characters, but smarmy writing, syrupy, clichéd, contrived. Plot twists you could spot a mile away—quick, everyone pile into the car with the pregnant woman for a high speed chase! Oh what a shock, she goes into labor!<br /><br />I skimmed through the last part, intent on finishing but not really interested. Not in the same class as <a title="Patty Jane's House of Curl by Lorna Landvik" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16451.Patty_Jane_s_House_of_Curl">Patty Jane's House of Curl</a> or <a title="Your Oasis on Flame Lake by Lorna Landvik" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16450.Your_Oasis_on_Flame_Lake">Your Oasis on Flame Lake</a>. Apart from a few flickers, it was hard to believe it was the same author.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer69379747">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18016592912688315896">Tiny Tall Pine, MN sets the stage for a tale of friendship, tragedy, and hope. It also sets the stage for a Hollywood film: <em>Ike and Inga</em>.<br /><br />The focal point of this novel can be found in the gatherings at the Cup O’Delight Café. This is the heart and soul of Tall Pine and the home of the Tall Pine Polka. <br /><br />By the way, the Tall Pine Polka is not a dance; it is a state of mind. It is the sharing of one’s talents and the celebration of life in the company of good friends. Isn’t that wonderful?<br /><br />There isn’t</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText18016592912688315896">Tiny Tall Pine, MN sets the stage for a tale of friendship, tragedy, and hope. It also sets the stage for a Hollywood film: <em>Ike and Inga</em>.<br /><br />The focal point of this novel can be found in the gatherings at the Cup O’Delight Café. This is the heart and soul of Tall Pine and the home of the Tall Pine Polka. <br /><br />By the way, the Tall Pine Polka is not a dance; it is a state of mind. It is the sharing of one’s talents and the celebration of life in the company of good friends. Isn’t that wonderful?<br /><br />There isn’t room enough to describe all of the great characters and subplots in this novel. Plus, I don’t want to spoil any surprises. Just read and enjoy this warm and sweet novel of friendship in small town Minnesota.<br /><br /><br /><br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer8158942404332048001">I have seldom been as disappointed in a book as I was in this one. I read <em>Angry Housewives Eating Bon Bons</em> several years ago and loved it. I read <em>Patti Jane's House of Curl</em> later and thought it was pretty funny. I was delighted to find this book and looked forward to reading it. I tried to get into it during the first 3 or 4 chapters, skimmed through a few more - up to Chapter 14. It was just plain boring. No plot, no humor, no intriguing characters. I didn't want to waste any more time on it, s</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText8158942404332048001">I have seldom been as disappointed in a book as I was in this one. I read <em>Angry Housewives Eating Bon Bons</em> several years ago and loved it. I read <em>Patti Jane's House of Curl</em> later and thought it was pretty funny. I was delighted to find this book and looked forward to reading it. I tried to get into it during the first 3 or 4 chapters, skimmed through a few more - up to Chapter 14. It was just plain boring. No plot, no humor, no intriguing characters. I didn't want to waste any more time on it, so I abandoned it and added the book to my bag to donate to the local library book sale. </span>

  <a href="/user/show/18256476-tara" class="left imgcol" title="Tara"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1438615198p2/18256476.jpg" alt="Tara" /></a>

      <a href="/user/show/18256476-tara" class="user" title="Tara">Tara</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="did not like it">did not like it</span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/16447.The_Tall_Pine_Polka" title="Paperback 9780449003701" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">No one</span></div>

        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/18256476-tara?shelf=i-d-rather-swallow-razor-blades" class="actionLinkLite">i-d-rather-swallow-razor-blades</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1186366235">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11514662595902464600">Too boring and awful to finish<br /><br />This may be the worst book that I have ever read. If I could give it less than one star I would, for after having read almost half of it, I have emerged from it's pages irritated and even worse, BORED. If you are reading this, please do not get me wrong. I had no illusions that this would be akin to reading Hemingway or Twain, but had hopes that it would be in the same vein as Fannie Flagg or Julia Glass. That is, not something that will exactly challenge your belie</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText11514662595902464600">Too boring and awful to finish<br /><br />This may be the worst book that I have ever read. If I could give it less than one star I would, for after having read almost half of it, I have emerged from it's pages irritated and even worse, BORED. If you are reading this, please do not get me wrong. I had no illusions that this would be akin to reading Hemingway or Twain, but had hopes that it would be in the same vein as Fannie Flagg or Julia Glass. That is, not something that will exactly challenge your beliefs or change your world viewpoint, but something that will be homespun and heart warming, which I am occasionally in the mood to read. This book was neither. It had none of the vitality or heart that you would typically find in the books of either Flagg or Glass. The characters in this story were either mundane or annoying, or caricatures (could Frau Katte's character be any more stereotypical?). The story was trite and not a bit of life emanated from the one-dimensional characters that populated it. Also, whoever did the editing for this book did Ms. Landvik no favors. Sentences ramble on and on, poorly constructed and terribly punctuated like an elderly aunt suffering severe dementia. Inaccurate abbreviations and word usages also pop up in abandon to join in this mess of a book. Lastly, the 'heroine' of this story is unlikable, so much so that I found myself not even caring what happened to her at all. The story line is amateurish at best and excruciatingly tedious and idiotic at worst. Honestly, the writing here is so sophomoric that I'm shocked that this was even published. This book is to literature what Etch-A-Sketch is to architecture.<br /><br />I tried longer than I should have to finish this book out of sheer stubbornness. All I have to show for that is seven days of my life that I will never get back and a loathing for anything else Lorna Landvik has written (this was my first experience reading her). If mindless reading (emphasis on mindless) is what you are looking for, have at it. As far as I am concerned, I have read backs of ketchup packages at fast food restaurants that provided more scintillation and enjoyment than this pathetic excuse of a book. If I liked it even slightly I would donate it to my local library. As it is, I'll be looking for the nearest waste bin to toss it into.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="11514662595902464600">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_848664820">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/848664820" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1616365-marleen" class="left imgcol" title="Marleen"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1451481453p2/1616365.jpg" alt="Marleen" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/848664820?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Apr 14, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1616365-marleen" class="user" title="Marleen">Marleen</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/1040543.The_Tall_Pine_Polka" title="Paperback 9780553817300" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/1616365-marleen?shelf=lorna-landvik" class="actionLinkLite">lorna-landvik</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer848664820">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3488840342898004293">The Tall Pine Polka is a charming little story. It has endearing aspects to it, the friendships, the sense of community, the forgiveness, and the bravery, and on the other hand it has more life-altering aspects to it; people getting sick, people dying, people cheating, etc. The ending is so beautiful, I felt the author redeemed herself for having wasted our time - now and then - with silly trivia prior to that.<br />At the same time this is probably Lorna Landvik’s most confusing book. What I mean by</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText3488840342898004293">The Tall Pine Polka is a charming little story. It has endearing aspects to it, the friendships, the sense of community, the forgiveness, and the bravery, and on the other hand it has more life-altering aspects to it; people getting sick, people dying, people cheating, etc. The ending is so beautiful, I felt the author redeemed herself for having wasted our time - now and then - with silly trivia prior to that.<br />At the same time this is probably Lorna Landvik’s most confusing book. What I mean by that is that there were quite many over-the-top characters, and unfortunately we didn’t get to truly know them. The story line wasn’t particular strong, still it was poignant at times. During the first 150 pages I didn’t see where the story was going. I'll admit I like the multiple ordinary small-town characters this author brings to life in her books. I’ve read most of her books, and I think Landvik has an immense talent, but here I felt these characters didn’t get the time to actually blossom on the page, as I think they deserved. Take Bill for instance, or Pete for that matter; there was more to these men than what we could discover (in the book), at least that’s what I felt. <br />My favorite character was definitely Harry, the Hollywood producer. I loved him! I could see him running around his office in his stockings and giving off sparks of static electricity on the carpet. He's an original.<br /><br />From back cover:<br />"In the small town of Tall Pine, Minnesota, at the Cup O'Delight Cafe, the townsfolk gather for what they call the Tall Pine Polka, an event in which heavenly coffee, good food, and that feeling of being alive among friends inspires both body and soul to dance. There's the cafe owner, the robust and beautiful Lee O'Leary, who escaped to the northwoods from an abusive husband; Miss Penk and Frau Katt, the town's only lesbian couple ('Well, we're za only ones who admit it.'); Pete, proprietor of the Shoe Shack, who spends nights crafting beautiful shoes to present to Lee, along with his declarations of love; Mary, whose bad poetry can clear out the cafe in seconds flat; and most important of all, Lee's best friend, Fenny Ness, a smart and sassy twenty-two-year-old going on eighty.<br />When Hollywood rolls into Tall Pine to shoot a movie, and a handsome musician known as Big Bill appears on the scene, Lee and Fenny find their friendship put to the test, as events push their hearts in unexplored directions-where endings can turn into new beginnings."</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="3488840342898004293">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <a href="/user/show/1741420-bea" class="user" title="Bea">Bea</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer287731770">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6552965371672226654">This is a story of the regulars who frequented The Cup O'Delight Cafe in Tall Pine, Minnesota. The Tall Pine Polka is a gathering of those regulars at the cafe after hours to drink the coffee, share food, and to dance. It is a time of good fellowship among frineds. <br /><br />Some of the characters are Lee O'Leary, who owns the cafe and who escaped (or thought she did) from an abusive husband to land in Tall Pine. Miss Penk and Frau Katt are the town's lesbian couple whose devotion to each other is strong</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6552965371672226654">This is a story of the regulars who frequented The Cup O'Delight Cafe in Tall Pine, Minnesota. The Tall Pine Polka is a gathering of those regulars at the cafe after hours to drink the coffee, share food, and to dance. It is a time of good fellowship among frineds. <br /><br />Some of the characters are Lee O'Leary, who owns the cafe and who escaped (or thought she did) from an abusive husband to land in Tall Pine. Miss Penk and Frau Katt are the town's lesbian couple whose devotion to each other is strong enough to deal with Miss Penk's injury. Pete, a shoemaker, is secretly in love with Lee and creates beautiful shoes for her but is too shy to tell her of his love. Mary wants to be accepted by the town but her bad poetry is barely tolerated by the regulars. And, Lee's best friend, Fenny Ness, is looking for her own love...and life.<br /><br />And, into this idyllic community, rolls Hollywood with all its temptations and also a handsome roaming nusician. The scene is set for the friendship between Lee and Fenny to be put to the test and for new beginnings to be discovered as each of the regulars deals with the aftermath of the events that started with a movie shoot in their town.<br /><br />I really enjoyed these characters. I alternated for whom I cheered on as each one's story pulled at my heart's strings. I want to visit and perhaps stay in Tall Pine. I liked this town and its people.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="6552965371672226654">...more</a>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_17662757">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/17662757" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/987336-sarah" class="left imgcol" title="Sarah"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1205501395p2/987336.jpg" alt="Sarah" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/17662757?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Mar 23, 2008</a>

      <a href="/user/show/987336-sarah" class="user" title="Sarah">Sarah</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/16447.The_Tall_Pine_Polka" title="Paperback 9780449003701" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/987336-sarah?shelf=general-fiction" class="actionLinkLite">general-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer17662757">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer265487919411320580">Every time I go into a bookstore or library I check to see if certain authors have released any new books (fingers crossed, oh please! Oh please!) So I was delighted when The Tall Pine Polka was released. I had gobbled up both Patty Jane's House of Curl and Your Oasis on Flame Lake and was hungrily awaiting another novel from Landvik, who has become one of my all-time favorite authors. As with previous Landvik works, Polka iss et in a small lakeside town in Minnesota. the majority of the charact</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText265487919411320580">Every time I go into a bookstore or library I check to see if certain authors have released any new books (fingers crossed, oh please! Oh please!) So I was delighted when The Tall Pine Polka was released. I had gobbled up both Patty Jane's House of Curl and Your Oasis on Flame Lake and was hungrily awaiting another novel from Landvik, who has become one of my all-time favorite authors. As with previous Landvik works, Polka iss et in a small lakeside town in Minnesota. the majority of the characters are of Scandinavian descent (with names like Lars Larson and references to delicacies such as lutefisk.) The story is reminiscent of Fannie Flagg's Welcome to the World Baby Girl! with snatches of Buster's Midnight Cafe by Sandra Dallas and Billie Lett's The Honk and Holler Opening Soon. While the plot itself is a little unrealistic (the central character is "discovered" and becomes an overnight Hollywood star) any thoughts of disbelief are sure to disappear as the reader becomes engrossed in the lives of Tall Pine's residents (and the movie makers that invade the town.) But it is the characters that shine here. Once again Landvik has created quirky people 9characters are an apt description0 whom the reader yearns to know. Fenny Ness, the beautiful, orphaned, twenty-two year old is someone that would be easy to hate except...except that you like her so much! Her best friend, Lee O'Leary, owner of a cafe called Cup O'Delight, will be familiar to all. The type of woman who is funny, talented and decent yet lacks the conventional beauty to score love and acceptance in most corners of our society. The "co-stars" add color tot he mix. There's Vietnam veteran Slim who barks like a dog when adequate words fail him. Harry Freed, the film producer, who gives nephew Christian's Ike and Inga movie script the go-ahead, stereotypical money-hungry Hollywood wanna-bes. Ms. Penk and Frau Katte, the town's only openly lesbian couple, blunt and headstrong, bent on dispensing their opinions solicited or not. Mary Gore (no relation to good ol'Al) keeps the Cup O'Delight regulars up to date through issues of her literary magazine, Angel Motors, of which she is self-appointed editor and its only contributor. Tall Pine's mayor, his pal Heine Osterberg and sweet Pete, proprietor of the Shoe Shack also stop in daily for a cup of joe and the latest gossip. And yes, of course, there is a love interest, Big Bill. A (gasp!) visitor tot he town, he quickly becomes one of the gang and is embroiled in one of the book's numerous love triangles. There are no big surprises here. Just a wholesome, pleasurable read that is sure to leave the reader craving coffee and chitchat with the Polka gang. I laughed, I cried, I pooped my pants..."Huh?" Just read the book, you'll find out what I mean. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="265487919411320580">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_95817958">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/95817958" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1402123-laurel-rain" class="left imgcol" title="Laurel-Rain"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1446954317p2/1402123.jpg" alt="Laurel-Rain" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/95817958?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Oct 16, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1402123-laurel-rain" class="user" title="Laurel-Rain">Laurel-Rain</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/1040543.The_Tall_Pine_Polka" title="Paperback 9780553817300" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer95817958">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5283773507989099883">Tall Pine, Minnesota has a lot to recommend it: quirky townsfolk who share traits that can be defined as folksy, friendly, nosy, and any number of other adjectives. But what really connects the residents of this town near the Canadian border is their unique gathering place known as the Cup O'Delight Café, made famous for its delicious coffee made with a secret blend known only to its owner, Lee O'Leary.<br /><br />We meet many of the residents in the opening pages, as they enter the café and order breakfast</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText5283773507989099883">Tall Pine, Minnesota has a lot to recommend it: quirky townsfolk who share traits that can be defined as folksy, friendly, nosy, and any number of other adjectives. But what really connects the residents of this town near the Canadian border is their unique gathering place known as the Cup O'Delight Café, made famous for its delicious coffee made with a secret blend known only to its owner, Lee O'Leary.<br /><br />We meet many of the residents in the opening pages, as they enter the café and order breakfast or lunch, or saunter in for polka night. Residents like Fenny Ness, who is "discovered" by a Hollywood producer, and who eventually stars in a movie made right in Tall Pine called "Ike and Inga." Mary is known for her bad poetry and her many annoying ways, while Pete is the proprietor of the Shoe Shack and has his special place at the counter every day.<br /><br />When the movie is shot in their little town, the lives of the residents will change forever. Some changes will include love alliances sparked during that time. What will draw Fenny to a recent newcomer in town known as Big Bill, and what will his presence in town do to the friendship between Fenny and Lee? How will the various comings and goings of the residents as they try to recover after a tragic event in the café ultimately affect the character of the town? And how will things finally settle into some kind of normalcy again?<br /><br />Filled with colorful characters, "The Tall Pine Polka (Ballantine Reader's Circle)" is reminiscent of other such tomes that spotlight a town as if it, too, is a character in the drama. Without the backdrop of Tall Pine, none of the characters would be nearly as interesting. And without the Hollywood presence, the daily lives of the characters might seem intriguing and quirky for awhile, but they would lack that special something. I thought the book went on too long and included too many unnecessary details of the movie-making process. Otherwise, it was pleasant, warm, and even memorable. Four stars. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="5283773507989099883">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer96062299">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10750759442911898106">Lorna Landvik, author of <em>Angry Housewives Eating Bon Bons</em>, has written a book about the residents of Tall Pine, Minnesota. Main character, Fenny Ness, is perfectly content in her small town until she gets cast as the leading role in a movie being filmed in Tall Pine. Life for all the characters in the small town is turned upside-down by the film crew.<br /><br />This book was light and fun. Just the kind of book that a reader should just breeze through but, for some reason, it took a real commitment of time</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText10750759442911898106">Lorna Landvik, author of <em>Angry Housewives Eating Bon Bons</em>, has written a book about the residents of Tall Pine, Minnesota. Main character, Fenny Ness, is perfectly content in her small town until she gets cast as the leading role in a movie being filmed in Tall Pine. Life for all the characters in the small town is turned upside-down by the film crew.<br /><br />This book was light and fun. Just the kind of book that a reader should just breeze through but, for some reason, it took a real commitment of time for me. It was an entertaining read, but not superb. In many ways this book reminded me of <em>The Bean Trees</em> by Barbara Kingsolver (although not as good!). Like <em>Bean Trees<em>, <em>The Tall Pine Polka</em> is filled with quirky and entertaining characters. The surprising plot, with all its twists and turns revolves around these likable people, and the ending wraps the story up in a nice little package. Worth reading.<br /><br />I read this book three months ago and I think back on it fondly.</em></em></span>

  <span style="display:none" id="freeText10298154938234784234">Lorna Landvik has a special way of making small town characters come alive!!<br /><br />From back cover:<br /><br />"In the small town of Tall Pine, Minnesota, at the Cup O'Delight Cafe, the townsfolk gather for what they call the Tall Pine Polka, an event in which heavenly coffee, good food, and that feeling of being alive among friends inspires both body and soul to dance. There's the cafe owner, the robust and beautiful Lee O'Leary, who escaped to the northwoods from an abusive husband; Miss Penk and Frau Katt, the town's only lesbian couple ('Well, we're za only ones who admit it.'); Pete, proprietor of the Shoe Shack, who spends nights crafting beautiful shoes to present to Lee, along with his declarations of love; Mary, whose bad poetry can clear out the cafe in seconds flat; and most important of all, Lee's best friend, Fenny Ness, a smart and sassy twenty-two-year-old going on eighty.<br /><br />When Hollywood rolls into Tall Pine to shoot a movie, and a handsome musician known as Big Bill appears on the scene, Lee and Fenny find their friendship put to the test, as events push their hearts in unexplored directions-where endings can turn into new beginnings."<br /><br /><br /><br /><br /></span>

  <a href="/user/show/640637-colleen" class="left imgcol" title="Colleen"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1209861444p2/640637.jpg" alt="Colleen" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/29056989?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Aug 02, 2008</a>

      <a href="/user/show/640637-colleen" class="user" title="Colleen">Colleen</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/16447.The_Tall_Pine_Polka" title="Paperback 9780449003701" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/640637-colleen?shelf=reviewed" class="actionLinkLite">reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer29056989">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11436421799967459029">I liked this book, but not as much as I really wanted to, and nowhere near as much as I enjoyed some of Landvik's other offerings. Though the cast of characters was initially interesting, they all seemed a little too eccentric as the novel progressed. The movie in a small town element was done better in the movie State and Main, and I for one thought there were too many subplots running throughout the novel which overcomplicated it all. <br /><br />I did think that Fenny, Bill and Lee were well-drawn, devel</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText11436421799967459029">I liked this book, but not as much as I really wanted to, and nowhere near as much as I enjoyed some of Landvik's other offerings. Though the cast of characters was initially interesting, they all seemed a little too eccentric as the novel progressed. The movie in a small town element was done better in the movie State and Main, and I for one thought there were too many subplots running throughout the novel which overcomplicated it all. <br /><br />I did think that Fenny, Bill and Lee were well-drawn, developed characters, but found the entire ex-husband/abuse story line deserved more inital attention especially given its sudden importance halfway though the story. The Hollywood people all seemed fairly shallowly drawn, and poor Boyd never really got the development he deserved.<br /><br />Truthfully, even a mediocre Landvik novel is better than a lot of other books out there, but I was disappointed that this novel didn't live up to her usual high standards. Probably deserves a 3.5 if we had that option.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="11436421799967459029">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer9538461765245151951">I fell in love with the characters in this book. There's Slim, the Vietnam vet who barks like a dog. Who wouldn't love an interesting guy like that? Then there's Lee, a chubby cafe owner who made a great escape from a mean and perhaps a little crazy ex husband. There's Fenny, whose parents were great explorers but she seems to be afraid. We have Big Bill, whose Aunt Mae Little Feather is upset that he might dilute his native American blood. In this small town there is also a lesbian couple and a</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText9538461765245151951">I fell in love with the characters in this book. There's Slim, the Vietnam vet who barks like a dog. Who wouldn't love an interesting guy like that? Then there's Lee, a chubby cafe owner who made a great escape from a mean and perhaps a little crazy ex husband. There's Fenny, whose parents were great explorers but she seems to be afraid. We have Big Bill, whose Aunt Mae Little Feather is upset that he might dilute his native American blood. In this small town there is also a lesbian couple and an aspiring poetess. Hollywood comes calling to this small town. Throw in a few twists like a love triangle and a movie star and you have a very interesting read. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer10141135277462244194">I am wavering between 3 and 4 stars on this one. I loved the writing style - tongue in cheek, omniscient narrator - but the characters weren't my favorite, or maybe they just didn't seem believable to me. At the risk of giving anything away, I didn't like the love triangle and Big Bill didn't impress me (maybe because he has no life savings?). I liked the idea of a small town- the Hollywood storyline was entertaining as well - and you can tell the author has inside knowledge of how it all works.</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText10141135277462244194">I am wavering between 3 and 4 stars on this one. I loved the writing style - tongue in cheek, omniscient narrator - but the characters weren't my favorite, or maybe they just didn't seem believable to me. At the risk of giving anything away, I didn't like the love triangle and Big Bill didn't impress me (maybe because he has no life savings?). I liked the idea of a small town- the Hollywood storyline was entertaining as well - and you can tell the author has inside knowledge of how it all works.<br /><br />I'd read more of Lorna Landvik and hopefully the romances in her other stories are more believable.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer15345487738939362044">I liked this book well enough, although I have to say right up front, if I was a character in that book, I would not have liked the main character, Fanny Ness, whom most everyone seems to adore.   <span style="display:none" id="freeText15345487738939362044">I liked this book well enough, although I have to say right up front, if I was a character in that book, I would not have liked the main character, Fanny Ness, whom most everyone seems to adore. She seems to me to be a self-centered, selfish, petulant, uncaring little brat.<br /><br />That said, the book was entertaining enough but almost formulaic -- small northern Minnesota town, eccentric townsfolk, Hollywood movie invades small town, and, well, I'm sure you can guess the rest. <br /><br />A light read, generally enjoyable, but not a whole lot to talk about when you're through reading it. </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a href="/review/show/51045546?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Apr 05, 2009</a>

      <a href="/user/show/804942-ali" class="user" title="Ali">Ali</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer51045546">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1821547397839248002">This novel is a lovely big friendly book, lots of characters you care about, and feel instantly at home with. The story of the people of Tall Pine,Minnesota and that of the film people who for a short time become a part of Tall Pine is a real rollercoaster, funny, sad and dramatic. The story highlights (if it needed highlighting) just how stupid the whole celebrity thing is - that the whole world is obessed with these days. Those things which are really important are more basic and everyday than</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText1821547397839248002">This novel is a lovely big friendly book, lots of characters you care about, and feel instantly at home with. The story of the people of Tall Pine,Minnesota and that of the film people who for a short time become a part of Tall Pine is a real rollercoaster, funny, sad and dramatic. The story highlights (if it needed highlighting) just how stupid the whole celebrity thing is - that the whole world is obessed with these days. Those things which are really important are more basic and everyday than Hollywood glamour - and Fenny's dealings with the media are hilarious.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="1821547397839248002">...more</a>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked &amp;&amp; exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;name=' + shelf_name + '&amp;a=' + action + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('gkBQtUVvw8Fngp2m4/o+duZj5JQpe61ouv4B9++3SJjnlG9mt73XO+ta6R2dm9jEr5QnjWCm6sLQ9wRlIyK+3Q==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&amp;book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;refresh=true' + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('XsYf5KawBbZGbdtFoTy6mAfWEinNgVnmuQivJ2EtZ147EiA3VGIRTMq1r/7fXVwqTiHRMIRcHkzTAaq1rbiRGw==')})
  }

Accused by the grieving family and the enraged townspeople, Letitia quickly sends her twelve-year-old daughter, Sally, out to hide in the brush before she is taken into custody. The angry mob would get revenge when they drag Letitia from her jail cell and hang her that very night. But they wouldn’t get Sally.Baby Allen, a courageous social worker, is assigned to Sally’s case, and gradually coaxes the young girl out of hiding, wins her trust, and secures her protection. But once Sally is safe, Baby is left with the greater mission of uncovering the truth about who is responsible for the infant’s death—a shocking revelation that will change the ways and attitudes of a town that has been long in need of changing. Just moments after four o’clock, a large split of snow separates from Jubilee Mountain high above the tiny hamlet and hurtles down the rocky slope, enveloping everything in its path including nine young children who are walking home from school. But only four children survive. Whiter Than Snow takes you into the lives of each of these families: There’s Lucy and Dolly Patch—two sisters, long estranged by a shocking betrayal. Joe Cobb, Swandyke’s only black resident, whose love for his daughter Jane forces him to flee Alabama. There’s Grace Foote, who hides secrets and scandal that belies her genteel façade. And Minder Evans, a civil war veteran who considers his cowardice his greatest sin. Finally, there’s Essie Snowball, born Esther Schnable to conservative Jewish parents, but who now works as a prostitute and hides her child’s parentage from all the world. Ultimately, each story serves as an allegory to the greater theme of the novel by echoing that fate, chance, and perhaps even divine providence, are all woven into the fabric of everyday life. And it’s through each character’s defining moment in his or her past that the reader understands how each child has become its parent’s purpose for living.     <div class=" clearFloats bigBox" id="aboutAuthor"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/10020.Lorna_Landvik">About Lorna Landvik</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
      <a href="/author/show/10020.Lorna_Landvik"><img alt="10020" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/authors/1323279367p2/10020.jpg" class="right" /></a>
    <div class="readable">
      
<span id="freeTextContainer14708257992792157582">Lorna Landvik is a mother of two and wife of one. She is the author of eight novels, including the best-selling ANGRY HOUSEWIVES EATING BON BONS, PATTY JANE'S HOUSE OF CURL and OH MY STARS. Also an<br />actor and playwright, Lorna has appeared in many stage productions. She is a new and passionate neophyte to the practice of yoga, which is a fine antidote to her long established practice of lounging. </span>

    </div>
